If you don’t plan on overclocking your PC, then an air-cooled CPU heatsink will be sufficient.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIf you like to push the limits by overclocking your components, we recommend water cooling your customized PC. Pre-built water cooling kits (called All-in-Ones or AiO water cooling) are the best option for beginners because you only need to mount them. There are no worries about filling and building. Simply mount the radiator and block inside your PC, and you’re on your way.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFor experienced builders, a \u003Ca class='link-more' href='https:\u002F\u002Fwww.newegg{0}\u002Fp\u002Fpl?N=100074981%20600036012'\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EDIY water cooling kit\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E with individual parts offers more flexibility. A typical DIY water cooling kit consists of a radiator, hoses, pump, water block, reservoir, and fan. When these pieces are installed and working together, they are called a loop and are very similar to what you would find under the hood of your car.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E"},{"question":"Do you need a Battery Backup (UPS) when building a custom PC?","answerHtml":"\u003Cp\u003EYes, adding a \u003Ca class='link-more' href='https:\u002F\u002Fwww.newegg.com\u002FBattery-Backup-UPS\u002FSubCategory\u002FID-72'\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EBattery Backup (UPS)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is a smart decision when building a custom PC, especially if you rely on your system for gaming, work, or critical tasks. A UPS provides backup power during outages, ensuring that your system doesn't shut down unexpectedly, preventing data loss and potential damage to hardware. It also protects against power surges and fluctuations, which can harm sensitive components like your motherboard and GPU. When selecting a UPS, ensure it’s capable of handling the power requirements of your custom build, which can be easily calculated using a power supply
